# Task: Analyze Test Coverage Gaps in Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

**Repository:** envoyproxy/envoy
**Output:** Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`

## Objective

Identify test coverage gaps in Envoy's HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) filter chain implementation. The HCM is the core HTTP processing pipeline in Envoy, responsible for routing, filter execution, and response handling.

## Scope

Focus on the HCM implementation in `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` and its test file `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc`. Also consider:
- `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` — filter chain execution
- `source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` — header manipulation

## Content Expectations

Your analysis must:
1. **Identify at least 5 specific untested code paths** in the HCM (with file + approximate line references)
2. **Propose a concrete test case** for each gap (test name, setup, assertions)
3. **Explain why each gap matters** (what bugs could slip through)
4. **Prioritize by risk**: label each gap as HIGH / MEDIUM / LOW

## Output Format

Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md` with this structure:

```markdown
# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

## Summary
[Brief overview of the most critical gaps found]

## Coverage Gaps

### Gap 1: [Title]
- **File**: source/common/http/...
- **Lines**: ~NNN-NNN
- **Risk**: HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW
- **Description**: [What code path is untested]
- **Proposed Test**: [Test name and approach]
- **Why It Matters**: [Potential bugs if untested]

[Repeat for gaps 2-5+]

## File References
[List of key files analyzed]
```

## Anti-Requirements
- Do not fabricate file paths or function names — inspect the actual codebase
- Do not list gaps without proposing concrete test cases
- Do NOT run the tests yourself — write the test file and the evaluation system validates independently

I am thinking...: Now I have the full picture of the `HeaderList::removeIf` method. There are TWO branches:
1. If lazy_map is non-empty: uses the map to iterate and remove
2. If lazy_map is empty: iterates directly over the list

The `RemovePrefix` test adds 5 non-inline headers (`addReference`). Looking at `HeaderList::insert`:
```cpp
template <class Key, class... Value> HeaderNode insert(Key&& key, Value&&... value) {
    ...
    if (!lazy_map_.empty()) {
        lazy_map_[i->key().getStringView()].push_back(i);
    }
    ...
}
```

The lazy_map only gets populated during `insert` if it's already non-empty. The map is built by `maybeMakeMap()`. So if `maybeMakeMap()` is never called before the 5 inserts, the lazy map remains empty, and the first call to `removePrefix` would call `removeIf` which would take the else-branch (lazy map empty).

## What the document covers

The 800-line analysis identifies **8 confirmed coverage gaps** across the three source files. Here is a precise executive summary of each:

---

### Gap 1 — `isPrematureRstStream` + `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` (conn_manager_impl.cc:677–748)
**Risk: 🔴 High**  
Both functions have **zero unit-test hits** (`grep` confirmed). They are called from `doDeferredStreamDestroy`/`onResetStream` but only exercised by integration tests that cannot verify individual branches. Five distinct sub-branches are untested: the "long-lived stream" early return, the "response code present" return, the `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` idempotency guard, the RST-ratio arithmetic, and the `doConnectionClose("too_many_premature_resets")` abort. This is the core RST-flood defence; a regression here is a security vulnerability.

---

### Gap 2 — `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` non-graceful path + `go_away_sent_` guard (conn_manager_impl.cc:797–823)
**Risk: 🟠 Medium-High**  
Only `graceful=true` is exercised (one test, line 5278). The `else` block — `shutdownNotice()`, `goAway()`, and `doConnectionClose("forced_goaway")` — is never called. The `go_away_sent_` guard's idempotency for the non-graceful path is also untested, leaving a potential double-close / double-GOAWAY bug undetected.

---

### Gap 3 — HTTP/1.0 `Connection: keep-alive` header (conn_manager_impl.cc:1938–1948)
**Risk: 🟡 Medium**  
All three HTTP/1.0 unit tests respond without a `Content-Length`, so `setShouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion(true)` is always called. The inner branch that emits `Connection: keep-alive` (line 1946–1948) is reached only when `Content-Length` is present, a scena

"void ConnectionManagerImpl::maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets() {\n  // If the connection has been drained due to premature resets, do not check this again.\n  // Without this flag, recursion may occur, as shown in the following stack trace:\n  //\n  //   maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()\n  //   doConnectionClose()\n  //   resetAllStreams()\n  //   onResetStream()\n  //   doDeferredStreamDestroy()\n  //   maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()\n  //   ...\n  //\n  // The recursion will continue until all streams are destroyed. If there are many streams\n  // that may result in a stack overflow. This flag is used to avoid above recursion.\n  if (drained_due_to_premature_resets_) {\n    return;\n  }\n\n  if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ == 0) {\n    return;\n  }\n\n  const uint64_t limit =\n      runtime_.snapshot().getInteger(ConnectionManagerImpl::PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey, 500);\n\n  if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit) {\n    // Even though the total number of streams have not reached `limit`, check if the number of bad\n    // streams is high enough that even if every subsequent stream is good, the connection\n    // would be closed once the limit is reached, and if so close the connection now.\n    if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < limit) {\n      return;\n    }\n  } else {\n    if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_) {\n      return;\n    }\n  }\n\n  if (read_callbacks_->connection().state() == Network::Connection::State::Open) {\n    stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.inc();\n\n    // Mark the the connection has been drained due to too many premature resets.\n    drained_due_to_premature_resets_ = true;\n\n    doConnectionClose(Network::ConnectionCloseType::Abort, absl::nullopt,\n                      \"too_many_premature_resets\");\n  }"

"void ConnectionManagerImpl::sendGoAwayAndClose(bool graceful) {\n  ENVOY_CONN_LOG(trace, \"connection manager sendGoAwayAndClose was triggerred from filters.\",\n                 read_callbacks_->connection());\n  if (go_away_sent_) {\n    return;\n  }\n\n  // Use graceful drain sequence if graceful shutdown is requested.\n  // startDrainSequence() works for both HTTP/1 and HTTP/2:\n  // - HTTP/1: shutdownNotice() + goAway() provides graceful close\n  // - HTTP/2: shutdownNotice() sends GOAWAY with high stream ID, then goAway() sends final GOAWAY\n  if (graceful) {\n    if (drain_state_ == DrainState::NotDraining) {\n      startDrainSequence();\n    }\n    // Consider the \"go away\" process started once draining begins.\n    // The actual GOAWAY frame will be sent in onDrainTimeout(), but we want to\n    // prevent multiple calls to sendGoAwayAndClose() from starting multiple drain sequences.\n    go_away_sent_ = true;\n  } else {\n    // Immediate close - send GOAWAY and close immediately\n    codec_->shutdownNotice();\n    codec_->goAway();\n    go_away_sent_ = true;\n    doConnectionClose(Network::ConnectionCloseType::FlushWriteAndDelay, absl::nullopt,\n                      \"forced_goaway\");\n  }\n}"
